## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology (population dynamics)
**Analysis**: The target is dP_dt, the time-derivative of population size P, which is the standard setting for continuous-time population growth models in ecology. With only t and P available, the most likely relationships are autonomous or time-forced ordinary differential equations capturing per-capita growth, density dependence, and possible external inputs/harvesting.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Malthusian (exponential) growth ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P (unlimited resources; constant per-capita growth rate)
- Exponential growth with immigration/emigration: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 (net constant inflow/outflow independent of P)
- Quadratic density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P**2 (crowding reduces growth; simplest self-limitation)
- Logistic growth (ODE form): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) (carrying capacity behavior with K = 1/c1)
- Generalized/theta-logistic: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P**c2) (variable strength/shape of density dependence)
- Power-law self-limitation: dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P**c2 (nonlinear crowding; c2>1 gives stronger high-density suppression)
- Gompertz growth (ODE form): dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) (logarithmic feedback; often for tumor/microbial growth slowing)
- Richards-type per-capita regulation: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - exp(c1 * log(c2 * P))) (flexible sigmoid regulation; Richards family expressed via log/exp)
- Allee effect (strong) with carrying capacity: dP_dt = c0 * P * (c1 * P - 1) * (1 - c2 * P) (reduced growth at low P; threshold at P=1/c1)
- Harvesting (proportional + constant): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 * P - c3 (mortality proportional to P plus constant catch/removal)
- Seasonally forced growth rate: dP_dt = P * (c0 + c1 * sin(c2 * t + c3)) (periodic environment modulates per-capita growth)
- Time-varying carrying capacity: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) + c2 * P * sin(c3 * t + c4) (effective K or crowding pressure fluctuates over time)
- Piecewise regulation via smooth switch: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * (c2 + tanh(c3 * (P - c4))) (different regimes below/above a density threshold)
- Autonomous per-capita polynomial: dP_dt = P * (c0 + c1 * P + c2 * P**2) (fits general per-capita growth-rate curve vs density)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Per-capita growth representation: expressing dP_dt as P * g(P,t) encodes births/deaths proportional to current population, with g capturing regulation/forcing.
- Carrying-capacity behavior: factors like (1 - c * P) or (1 - c * P**k) imply a stable equilibrium near P ≈ 1/c (or (1/c)^(1/k)) where growth changes sign.
- Crowding/self-limitation strength: presence of -c * P**2 (or higher powers) indicates increasing marginal suppression at high density; higher exponents steepen the decline.
- Allee thresholds: inclusion of a low-density factor like (c * P - 1) yields negative growth below P = 1/c and positive growth above it (bistability/critical mass).
- Log-feedback slowing: forms like P * log(c / P) imply diminishing per-capita growth roughly linearly with log(P), often producing asymmetric sigmoidal trajectories.
- External removals vs intrinsic regulation: subtractive constants (−c) suggest fixed harvesting/constant mortality, while subtractive terms proportional to P (−c*P) suggest per-capita mortality or proportional harvest.
- Seasonality/environmental forcing: additive sinusoidal terms in the per-capita rate, e.g., P*(c0 + c1*sin(c2*t)), indicate periodic variation in growth conditions.
- Multiple equilibria detection: products of linear factors in P (e.g., P*(c1*P-1)*(1-c2*P)) imply multiple fixed points; stability alternates as sign changes across roots.
- Regime-switching density dependence: tanh/logistic switching in P suggests different growth laws in low vs high density, approximating piecewise ecological regimes without hard discontinuities.

If c1=0: c0 + c2*P² + P^(1+c3) + c7*P. Set c3=-2/3, c0=0: c2*P² + P^(1/3) + c7*P. P^(1/3) coeff=1.
Candidate 41 verdict: [NO MATCH]

### Candidate 54: Complex rational. Let me expand:
`((P+c0)*(P*c1+c2) + (P*c3+c4)*(P^(1/3)*(P+c0)+P³*c5+P²*c6+P*c7))/((P+c0)*(P*c3+c4))`

= (P*c1+c2)/(P*c3+c4) + (P^(1/3)*(P+c0)+P³*c5+P²*c6+P*c7)/(P+c0)

Second part: P^(1/3) + (P³*c5+P²*c6+P*c7)/(P+c0). With proper constants this becomes P^(1/3)+α*P²+β*P.

First part: (c1*P+c2)/(c3*P+c4). This is a rational function that can be constant if c1/c3=c2/c4, giving value c1/c3. Set this to 0 (c1=c2=0): P^(1/3)+α*P²+β*P. P^(1/3) coeff=1.
Candidate 54 verdict: [NO MATCH]

### Candidate 55: `(P^(1/3)*(Pc0+c1)+sqrt(P)*c2*(Pc0+c1)+P²*c3*(Pc0+c1)+P*c4*(Pc0+c1)+P*c5+2P*(Pc0+c1)+c6*(Pc0+c1)+c7)/(Pc0+c1)`

= P^(1/3)+sqrt(P)*c2+c3*P²+c4*P+P*c5/(c0*P+c1)+2P+c6+c7/(c0*P+c1)

For P*c5/(c0*P+c1) + c7/(c0*P+c1) = (c5*P+c7)/(c0*P+c1). This is rational. For it to be constant: c5/c0 = c7/c1, giving value c5/c0. Set c5=c7=0, c2=0, c6=0: P^(1/3)+c3*P²+c4*P+2P. P^(1/3) coeff=1.
Candidate 55 verdict: [NO MATCH]
